## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma=stress, epsilon=strain, T=temperature) match constitutive relations used in elasticity, plasticity, and viscoplastic/creep models where stress depends on deformation and temperature-dependent stiffness/strength and thermal strain offsets.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (elastic response with temperature-dependent modulus and thermal expansion)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity (no thermal strain offset): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (elastic modulus varying with T)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial with T-dependent stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 + (c4 + c5 * T) * epsilon**3 (anharmonic elastic response, small-to-moderate strains)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type relation inverted (implicit plasticity surrogate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * Abs(sigma)**c3) (captures elastic + nonlinear inelastic strain; used as fit form when only epsilon,T are available)
- Ludwik/Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * (c3 * epsilon)**c4 * exp(c5 * T) (strain hardening modulated by T; exp(c5*T) can represent softening if c5<0)
- Voce (exponential) hardening with T dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening; yield/flow stress decreases with T if coefficients imply it)
- Swift hardening with T dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 + epsilon)**c3 (power-law hardening with pre-strain/offset; temperature affects strength via prefactor)
- Johnson–Cook-style (rate-ignored) plastic flow surrogate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (common metallurgy form; here the T-factor acts as thermal softening/hardening)
- Elastic–plastic bilinear (piecewise) with T-dependent yield and modulus: sigma = piecewise( (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, epsilon <= (c2 + c3 * T); (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 + c3 * T) + (c4 + c5 * T) * (epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T)), epsilon > (c2 + c3 * T) ) (captures yield + linear hardening, both temperature dependent)
- Thermally activated softening factor on a base stress–strain curve: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(c3 * T) (multiplicative temperature sensitivity; softening if c3<0)
- Logarithmic strain hardening with thermal shift: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * log(c4 * epsilon + c5) (captures rapid early hardening that tapers; often used empirically for metals/polymers)
- Hyperbolic tangent transition to flow with T-dependent scale: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * tanh((c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon) + c4 * epsilon (smooth elastic-to-plastic-like transition; useful as a regression-friendly constitutive surrogate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion induces a stress-free strain shift: structures like (epsilon - c * (T - c)) move the zero-stress point with temperature.
- Elastic modulus typically decreases with T in many solids: using (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2) multiplying epsilon captures stiffness softening/hardening trends.
- Yield/flow stress commonly drops with T: multiplicative temperature factors such as exp(c*T) (with c<0) or low-order polynomials in T on a base hardening law encode thermal softening.
- Strain hardening often follows power-law or saturating behavior: epsilon**c captures scale-free hardening; (1-exp(-c*epsilon)) captures saturation at large strain.
- A smooth elastic-to-plastic transition can be modeled without explicit yield detection using tanh(c*epsilon) or similar smooth transition functions to avoid non-differentiable kinks.
- If the material response changes curvature with strain (e.g., early rapid hardening then slower), log(c*epsilon+c) or mixed polynomial+log forms often fit better than pure polynomials.
- Temperature–strain interaction is frequently non-separable: allowing coefficients of epsilon, epsilon**2, etc. to depend on T (e.g., (c0+c1*T)*epsilon + (c2+c3*T)*epsilon**2) captures changes in hardening rate with temperature.

**GT:** `7.773814951275034*epsilon**3 + 55.12431765498469*epsilon**0.26636900997297436*exp(-52.48673409660327/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*3.8053996848046987*sin(T - 276.43885211152184)`

The GT has three terms:
1. **Term 1:** `c0 * epsilon^3` — a pure polynomial term in epsilon
2. **Term 2:** `c2 * epsilon^c3 * exp(-c4/(c5*T))` — epsilon to a fractional power (~0.266) times an Arrhenius-type exponential in 1/T
3. **Term 3:** `epsilon * c6 * sin(T - c7)` — epsilon times a sinusoidal function of T

Key structural features:
- The exponent c3 ≈ 0.2664 is close to 1/4 = 0.25 but NOT exactly 1/4
- The exponential is `exp(-const/T)`, an Arrhenius form
- The sin term is `sin(T - c7)` which can be expanded as `sin(T)cos(c7) - cos(T)sin(c7)`

**Critical observation:** c3 ≈ 0.2664 ≠ 0.25. The GT uses `epsilon^0.2664`, while candidates use `epsilon^(1/4) = epsilon^0.25`. These are fundamentally different basis functions — `epsilon^0.2664` and `epsilon^0.25` are NOT equivalent for all epsilon. So any candidate using `|epsilon|^(1/4)` as a substitute for `epsilon^c3` cannot be an exact match unless there's a free exponent parameter.

Also, `exp(-c/T)` (Arrhenius) vs `exp(c*T)` (linear exponential in T) — these are structurally different and cannot match.

Let me check each candidate for these structural requirements:

**Most candidates** have:
- `exp(T*c)` instead of `exp(-c/T)` — structurally different, NO MATCH
- `|epsilon|^(1/4)` instead of `epsilon^0.2664` — structurally different
- Various sin/cos terms

- **Candidate 39:** Has `exp(c4/T)` — this matches the Arrhenius form! Let me check more carefully.

**Candidate 8, 9, 33:** Have `(|epsilon|+1)^(c*sin(T*c+c))` — this is a very different functional form.

None of the candidates have both:
1. `exp(-const/T)` multiplied by `epsilon^(~0.266)`
2. `epsilon * sin(T - const)`
3. `epsilon^3`

in a way that can be made equivalent to the GT.

- Uses `exp(c*T)` instead of `exp(c/T)` 
- Has wrong basis functions (epsilon^(1/4) ≠ epsilon^0.2664)

- Missing essential structural components
